<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script>

<p>The <b>Human Development Index</b> (<b>HDI</b>) is a composite statistic of <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> indicators, which are used to rank countries into four tiers of <a href="/wiki/Human_development_(humanity)" title="Human development (humanity)">human development</a>. A country scores higher HDI when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" title="Life expectancy at birth">lifespan</a> is higher, the <a href="/wiki/Education" title="Education">education</a> level is higher, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP_per_capita" title="GDP per capita">GDP per capita</a> is higher, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fertility_rate" title="Fertility rate">fertility rate</a> is lower, and the <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">inflation</a> rate is lower. The HDI was developed by the Pakistani economist <a href="/wiki/Mahbub_ul_Haq" title="Mahbub ul Haq">Mahbub ul Haq</a> working alongside Indian economist <a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a>, often framed in terms of whether people are able to "be" and "do" desirable things in their life, and was published by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a>.</p>
<p>The 2010 <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Report" title="Human Development Report">Human Development Report</a> introduced an <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index</a> (IHDI). While the simple HDI remains useful, it stated that "the IHDI is the actual level of human development (accounting for <a href="/wiki/Social_inequality" title="Social inequality">inequality</a>)," and "the HDI can be viewed as an index of 'potential' human development (or the maximum IHDI that could be achieved if there were no inequality)."</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span></h2>


<p>The origins of the HDI are found in the annual Human Development Reports produced by the Human Development Reports Office of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> (UNDP). These were devised and launched by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pakistani" title="Pakistani">Pakistani</a> economist <a href="/wiki/Mahbub_ul_Haq" title="Mahbub ul Haq">Mahbub ul Haq</a> in 1990, and had the explicit purpose "to shift the focus of development economics from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_income" title="National income">national income</a> accounting to people-centered policies". To produce the Human Development Reports, Mahbub ul Haq formed a group of development economists including <a href="/wiki/Paul_Streeten" title="Paul Streeten">Paul Streeten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frances_Stewart" title="Frances Stewart">Frances Stewart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Ranis" title="Gustav Ranis">Gustav Ranis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Keith_Griffin_(economist)" title="Keith Griffin (economist)">Keith Griffin</a>, Sudhir Anand, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meghnad_Desai" title="Meghnad Desai">Meghnad Desai</a>. Working alongside Nobel laureate <a href="/wiki/Amartya_Sen" title="Amartya Sen">Amartya Sen</a>, they worked on capabilities and functions that provided the underlying conceptual framework. Haq was sure that a simple composite measure of human development was needed in order to convince the public, academics, and politicians that they can and should evaluate development not only by economic advances but also improvements in human <a href="/wiki/Well-being" title="Well-being">well-being</a>. Sen initially opposed this idea, but he was helped by Haq in order to develop the Index. Sen was worried that it was going to be difficult to capture the full complexity of human capabilities in a single index, but Haq requested him that only a single number would shift the immediate attention of politicians from economic to human well-being.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Dimensions_and_calculation">Dimensions and calculation</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_method_.282010_Report_onwards.29">New method (2010 Report onwards)</span></h3>
<p>Published on 4 November 2010 (and updated on 10 June 2011), the 2010 Human Development Report (HDI) combines three dimensions:</p>
<ul>
<li>A long and healthy life: Life expectancy at birth</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Education_index" title="Education index">Education index</a>: Mean years of schooling and Expected years of schooling</li>
<li>A decent standard of living: <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_income" title="Gross national income">GNI</a> per capita (<a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">PPP</a> US$)</li>
</ul>
<p>In its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2010_Human_Development_Report" title="2010 Human Development Report">2010 Human Development Report</a>, the UNDP began using a new method of calculating the HDI. The following three indices are used:</p>

<p><small>LE: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" title="Life expectancy at birth">Life expectancy at birth</a><br/>
MYS: Mean years of schooling (Years that a person 25 years-of-age or older has spent in schools)<br/>
EYS: Expected years of schooling (Years of schooling for children under 18 years of age)<br/>
GNIpc: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GNI_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GNI (PPP) per capita">Gross national income at purchasing power parity per capita</a></small></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Old_method_.28before_2010_Report.29">Old method (before 2010 Report)</span></h3>
<p>The HDI combined three dimensions last used in its 2009 Report:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> at birth, as an index of population health and longevity to HDI</li>
<li>Knowledge and education, as measured by the adult <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">literacy</a> rate (with two-thirds weighting) and the combined primary, secondary, and tertiary <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gross_enrollment_ratio" title="Gross enrollment ratio">gross enrollment ratio</a> (with one-third weighting).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living" title="Standard of living">Standard of living</a>, as indicated by the <a href="/wiki/Natural_logarithm" title="Natural logarithm">natural logarithm</a> of <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a> <a href="/wiki/Per_capita" title="Per capita">per capita</a> at <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>.</li>
</ul>

<p>This methodology was used by the UNDP until their 2011 report.</p>
<p>The formula defining the HDI is promulgated by the United Nations Development Programme (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNDP" title="UNDP">UNDP</a>). In general, to transform a raw <a href="/wiki/Variable_(mathematics)" title="Variable (mathematics)">variable</a>, say <span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
<mi>x</mi>
</mstyle>
</mrow>
<annotation encoding="application/x-tex">{\displaystyle x}</annotation>
</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/87f9e315fd7e2ba406057a97300593c4802b53e4" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; width:1.34ex; height:1.676ex;"/></span>, into a unit-free <a href="/wiki/Index_(economics)" title="Index (economics)">index</a> between 0 and 1 (which allows different indices to be added together), the following <a href="/wiki/Formula" title="Formula">formula</a> is used:</p>
<ul>
<li><span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>

<mtext> index</mtext>
</mrow>
<mo>=</mo>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
<mfrac>
<mrow>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mo form="prefix" movablelimits="true">min</mo>
<mrow>
<mo>(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>)</mo>
</mrow>
</mrow>
<mrow>
<mo form="prefix" movablelimits="true">max</mo>
<mrow>
<mo>(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>
<mo>)</mo>
</mrow>
<mo>−<!-- − --></mo>
<mo form="prefix" movablelimits="true">min</mo>
<mrow>
<mo>(</mo>
<mi>x</mi>

</semantics>
</math></span><img alt="x{\text{ index}}={\frac {x-\min \left(x\right)}{\max \left(x\right)-\min \left(x\right)}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5b880c0c3c0b2292b0331a9a0fcc8e199f7fc21d" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:29.639ex; height:6.509ex;"/></span></li>
</ul>
<p>where <span><span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
<semantics>
<mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

<semantics>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2015_Human_Development_Report">2015 Human Development Report</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">List of countries by Human Development Index</a></div>
<p>The 2015 Human Development Report by the United Nations Development Programme was released on December 14, 2015, and calculates HDI values based on estimates for 2014. Below is the list of the "very high human development" countries:</p>
<ul>
<li><img alt="Increase" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" title="Increase" width="11"/> = increase.</li>
<li><img alt="Steady" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" title="Steady" width="11"/> = steady.</li>
<li><img alt="Decrease" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" title="Decrease" width="11"/> = decrease.</li>
<li>The number in brackets represents the number of ranks the country has climbed (up or down) relative to the ranking in 2014 report.</li>
</ul>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_Human_Development_Report">2014 Human Development Report</span></h2>
<p>The 2014 Human Development Report by the United Nations Development Programme was released on July 24, 2014, and calculates HDI values based on estimates for 2013. Below is the list of the "very high human development" countries:</p>
<ul>
<li><img alt="Increase" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" title="Increase" width="11"/> = increase.</li>
<li><img alt="Steady" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" title="Steady" width="11"/> = steady.</li>
<li><img alt="Decrease" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" title="Decrease" width="11"/> = decrease.</li>
<li>The number in brackets represents the number of ranks the country has climbed (up or down) relative to the ranking in 2013 report.</li>
</ul>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI">Inequality-adjusted HDI</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI</a></div>
<p>The Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index (IHDI) is a "measure of the average level of human development of people in a society once inequality is taken into account."</p>
<p><small>Note: The green arrows (<img alt="Increase" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" title="Increase" width="11"/>), red arrows (<img alt="Decrease" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" title="Decrease" width="11"/>), and blue dashes (<img alt="Steady" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" title="Steady" width="11"/>) represent changes in rank. The changes in rank are not relative to the HDI list above, but are according to the source (p. 168) calculated with the exclusion of countries which are missing IHDI data.</small></p>

</ol>
</div>
<p>Countries in the top quartile of HDI ("very high human development" group) with a missing IHDI: <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_not_included">Countries not included</span></h3>
<p>Some countries were not included for various reasons, primarily due to the lack of necessary data. The following United Nations Member States were not included in the 2014 report: <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_Human_Development_Report">2013 Human Development Report</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">List of countries by Human Development Index</a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI_2">Inequality-adjusted HDI</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI</a></div>
<p>The Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index (IHDI) is a "measure of the average level of human development of people in a society once inequality is taken into account."</p>
<p><small>Note: The green arrows (<img alt="Increase" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" title="Increase" width="11"/>), red arrows (<img alt="Decrease" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" title="Decrease" width="11"/>), and blue dashes (<img alt="Steady" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" title="Steady" width="11"/>) represent changes in rank. The changes in rank are not relative to the HDI list above, but are according to the source (p. 152) calculated with the exclusion of countries which are missing IHDI data.</small></p>

<p>Countries in the top quartile of HDI ("very high human development" group) with a missing IHDI: <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2011_Human_Development_Report">2011 Human Development Report</span></h2>
<p>The 2011 Human Development Report was released on 2 November 2011, and calculated HDI values based on estimates for 2011. Below is the list of the "very high human development" countries (equal to the top <a href="/wiki/Quartile" title="Quartile">quartile</a>):</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI_3">Inequality-adjusted HDI</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI</a></div>
<p>Below is a list of countries in the top quartile by Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index (IHDI). According to the report, the IHDI is a "measure of the average level of human development of people in a society once inequality is taken into account."</p>
<p><small>Note: The green arrows (<img alt="Increase" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" title="Increase" width="11"/>), red arrows (<img alt="Decrease" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" title="Decrease" width="11"/>), and blue dashes (<img alt="Steady" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" title="Steady" width="11"/>) represent changes in rank when compared to the 2011 HDI list, for countries listed in both rankings.</small></p>

<p>Countries in the top quartile of HDI ("very high human development" group) with a <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_inequality-adjusted_HDI#Missing_data" title="List of countries by inequality-adjusted HDI">missing IHDI</a> include: <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_not_included_2">Countries not included</span></h3>
<p>Some countries were not included for various reasons, mainly the unavailability of certain crucial data. The following United Nations Member States were not included in the 2011 report: <a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2010_Human_Development_Report">2010 Human Development Report</span></h2>
<p>The 2010 Human Development Report by the United Nations Development Program was released on November 4, 2010, and calculates HDI values based on estimates for 2010. Below is the list of the "very high human development" countries:</p>
<p><small>Note: The green arrows (<img alt="Increase" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" title="Increase" width="11"/>), red arrows (<img alt="Decrease" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" title="Decrease" width="11"/>), and blue dashes (<img alt="Steady" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" title="Steady" width="11"/>) represent changes in rank when compared to the 2009 HDI published in the 2010 report.</small></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inequality-adjusted_HDI_4">Inequality-adjusted HDI</span></h3>
<p>The 2010 Human Development Report was the first to calculate an Inequality-adjusted Human Development Index (IHDI), which factors in inequalities in the three basic dimensions of human development (income, life expectancy, and education). Below is a list of countries in the top quartile by IHDI:</p>
<p><small>Note: The green arrows (<img alt="Increase" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" title="Increase" width="11"/>), red arrows (<img alt="Decrease" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" title="Decrease" width="11"/>), and blue dashes (<img alt="Steady" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" title="Steady" width="11"/>) represent changes in rank when compared to the 2010 HDI list, for countries listed in both rankings.</small></p>

</ol>
</div>
<p>Countries in the top quartile of HDI ("very high human development" group) with a missing IHDI include: <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" title="Republic of China">Republic of China</a> (<a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>), <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_not_included_3">Countries not included</span></h3>
<p>Some countries were not included for various reasons, mainly the unavailability of certain crucial data. The following United Nations Member States were not included in the 2010 report. <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> lodged a formal protest at its lack of inclusion. The UNDP explained that Cuba had been excluded due to the lack of an "internationally reported figure for Cuba's Gross National Income adjusted for Purchasing Power Parity". All other indicators for Cuba were available, and reported by the UNDP, but the lack of one indicator meant that no ranking could be attributed to the country. The situation has been addressed and, in later years, Cuba has ranked as a High Human Development country.</p>
<div>

</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2009_Human_Development_Report">2009 Human Development Report</span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index_(2009)" title="List of countries by Human Development Index (2009)">2009</a> <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Report" title="Human Development Report">Human Development Report</a> by the UNDP was released on October 5, 2009, and covers the period up to 2007. It was titled "Overcoming barriers: Human mobility and development". The top countries by HDI were grouped in a new category called "very high human development". The report refers to these countries as <b>developed countries</b>. They are:</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_not_included_4">Countries not included</span></h3>
<p>Some countries were not included for various reasons, such as being a non-UN member or unable or unwilling to provide the necessary data at the time of publication. Besides the <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">states with limited recognition</a>, the following states were also not included.</p>
<div>

</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2008_statistical_update">2008 statistical update</span></h2>
<p>A new index was released on December 18, 2008. This so-called "statistical update" covered the period up to 2006 and was published without an accompanying Human Development Report. The update is relevant due to newly released estimates of <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parities</a> (PPP), implying substantial adjustments for many countries, resulting in changes in HDI values and, in many cases, HDI ranks.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Countries_not_included_5">Countries not included</span></h3>
<p>Some countries were not included for various reasons, such as being a non-UN member, unable, or unwilling to provide the necessary data at the time of publication. Besides the states with limited recognition, the following states were also not included.</p>
<div>

</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="2007.2F2008_Human_Development_Report">2007/2008 Human Development Report</span></h2>
<p>The Human Development Report for 2007/2008 was launched in <a href="/wiki/Bras%C3%ADlia" title="Brasília">Brasília</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, on November 27, 2007. Its focus was on "Fighting climate change: Human solidarity in a divided world." Most of the data used for the report are derived largely from 2005 or earlier, thus indicating an HDI for 2005. Not all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_member_states" title="United Nations member states">UN member states</a> choose to or are able to provide the necessary statistics.</p>
<p>The report showed a small increase in world HDI in comparison with last year's report. This rise was fueled by a general improvement in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_countries" title="Developing countries">developing world</a>, especially of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Least_developed_countries" title="Least developed countries">least developed countries</a> group. This marked improvement at the bottom was offset with a decrease in HDI of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_income_countries" title="High income countries">high income countries</a>.</p>
<p>A HDI below 0.5 is considered to represent "low development". All 22 countries in that category are located in <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>. The highest-scoring Sub-Saharan countries, <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, are ranked 119th and 121st, respectively. Nine countries departed from this category this year and joined the "medium development" group.</p>
<p>A HDI of 0.8 or more is considered to represent "high development". This includes all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developed_countries" title="Developed countries">developed countries</a>, such as those in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oceania" title="Oceania">Oceania</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Asia" title="Eastern Asia">Eastern Asia</a>, as well as some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_countries" title="Developing countries">developing countries</a> in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_and_South_America" title="Central and South America">Central and South America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, and the oil-rich <a href="/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula" title="Arabian Peninsula">Arabian Peninsula</a>. Seven countries were promoted to this category this year, leaving the "medium development" group: <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>.</p>
<p>On the following table, green arrows (<img alt="Increase" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" title="Increase" width="11"/>) represent an increase in ranking over the previous study, while red arrows (<img alt="Decrease" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/11px-Decrease2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/17px-Decrease2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Decrease2.svg/22px-Decrease2.svg.png 2x" title="Decrease" width="11"/>) represent a decrease in ranking. They are followed by the number of spaces they moved. Blue dashes (<img alt="Steady" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="300" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/11px-Steady2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/17px-Steady2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Steady2.svg/22px-Steady2.svg.png 2x" title="Steady" width="11"/>) represent a nation that did not move in the rankings since the previous study.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Past_top_countries">Past top countries</span></h2>
<p>The list below displays the top-ranked country from each year of the Human Development Index. <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> has been ranked the highest twelve times, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> eight times, followed by <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> which has been ranked highest three times. <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> has been ranked highest twice.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_each_original_report">In each original report</span></h3>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span></h2>

<p>The Human Development Index has been criticized on a number of grounds including alleged ideological biases towards <a href="/wiki/Egalitarianism" title="Egalitarianism">egalitarianism</a> and so-called "<a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western</a> <a href="/wiki/Economic_system" title="Economic system">models of development</a>", failure to include any <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecological" title="Ecological">ecological</a> considerations, lack of consideration of technological development or contributions to the human civilization, focusing exclusively on national performance and ranking, lack of attention to development from a global perspective, measurement error of the underlying statistics, and on the UNDP's changes in formula which can lead to severe misclassification in the categorisation of 'low', 'medium', 'high' or 'very high' human development countries.</p>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Environmental_full-cost_accounting" title="Environmental full-cost accounting">Environmental full-cost accounting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Overconsumption" title="Overconsumption">Overconsumption</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecological_Debt_Day" title="Ecological Debt Day">Ecological Debt Day</a></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Economists" title="Economists">Economists</a> Hendrik Wolff, Howard Chong and <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_Auffhammer" title="Maximilian Auffhammer">Maximilian Auffhammer</a> discuss the HDI from the perspective of data error in the underlying health, education and income statistics used to construct the HDI. They identified three sources of data error which are due to (i) data updating, (ii) formula revisions and (iii) thresholds to classify a country's development status and conclude that 11%, 21% and 34% of all countries can be interpreted as currently misclassified in the development bins due to the three sources of data error, respectively. The authors suggest that the United Nations should discontinue the practice of classifying countries into development bins because - they claim - the cut-off values seem arbitrary, can provide incentives for strategic behavior in reporting official statistics, and have the potential to misguide politicians, investors, charity donors and the public who use the HDI at large. In 2010 the UNDP reacted to the criticism and updated the thresholds to classify nations as low, medium, and high human development countries. In a comment to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i> in early January 2011, the Human Development Report Office responded to a January 6, 2011 article in the magazine which discusses the Wolff <i>et al.</i> paper. The Human Development Report Office states that they undertook a systematic revision of the methods used for the calculation of the HDI and that the new methodology directly addresses the critique by Wolff <i>et al.</i> in that it generates a system for continuous updating of the human development categories whenever formula or data revisions take place.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geographical_coverage">Geographical coverage</span></h2>
<p>The HDI has extended its geographical coverage: David Hastings, of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Commission_for_Asia_and_the_Pacific" title="United Nations Economic and Social Commission for Asia and the Pacific">United Nations Economic and Social Commission for Asia and the Pacific</a>, published a report geographically extending the HDI to 230+ economies, whereas the UNDP HDI for 2009 enumerates 182 economies and coverage for the 2010 HDI dropped to 169 countries.</p>
